Article 111 of our constitution provides that the law declared by the Appellate Division shall be binding on the High Court Division and the law </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">declared by either Division of the Supreme Court</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> shall be binding on all courts subordinate to it.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Since the judgment and decree passed in the earlier suit was affirmed by the Appellate Division the present suit cannot be maintainable in view of the fact that as the suit is barred by law and law declared by </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">the Appellate Division in the judgment passed</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> in Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 1413 of 2002 is to be followed. ...(23 to 25)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 105%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 105%;">Islami Bank Bangladesh Vs. Abdul Jalil 53 DLR (2001)-29; Abdul Jalil and others Vs. Islaimi Bank 53 DLR (AD) (2001)-12; Shahjahan Siraj (Md) Vs. Md. Rafique Quoraishi and others 19 BLC (AD)-143; Abdul Jalil and others Vs. Islami Bank Bangladesh Ltd. and others 64 LDR (AD) 107; Sreemati Pushpa Rani Das and another Vs. A.K.M Habibur Rahman and others 13 BLD (AD)-217; Md. Mahbubul Haque Vs. Md. A. Kader Monshi 8 BLT (AD)-177 and Burmah Eastern Ltd. Vs. Burmah Eastern Employees Union 18 DLR (Dhaka)-709 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. Syed Mokaddas Ali, Advocate </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">- - - For the petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. Moin Uddin, Advocate with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr.</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> Md.</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> Kobad Hossain, Advocate</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. Abul Hossain, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">- - -For the opposite parties</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Md. Ashraful Kamal, J: </span></u></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">This Rule was issued calling upon the opposite parties to show cause as to why the order dated 13.10.2009 passed by the learned Joint District Judge, Court No. 3, Dhaka in Title Suit No. 164 of 2007 should not be set aside and/or pass such other or further order or orders as to this Court may seem fit and proper. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Brief facts, necessary for the disposal of this Rule, are as follows;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2(a).<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Opposite party No.1 as plaintiff had filed a Title Suit being No. 164 of 2007 in the Court of Joint District Judge, Court No.3, Dhaka for a declaration of title in respect of ‘ka’ schedule property to the plaint and recovery of khas possession with cancellation of registered sale deed dated 30.10.2005.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2(b).<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The facts of the case of the plaintiff-opposite party No.1 are that the government of the then East Pakistan allotted the property in question to one Md. Hanif Bhuiyan vide<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>registered deed No. 4015 dated 27.06.1957. Thereafter, Hanif Bhuiyan sold the property to the plaintiff’s mother Mrs. Firoza Begum vide registered sale deed No. 796 dated 11.02.1964. By constructing two building thereon Mrs. Firoja Begum had been living there with her family members. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2(c).<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">     </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">On 15.05.1992 mother of the plaintiffs made an oral gift in respect of the property in question in favour of the plaintiff and handed <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">over the possession. In such way the plaintiff has</span> been owing and possessing the suit property. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2(d).<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The plaintiff’s 3(three) sisters, (the defendant Nos. 2-4 to the plaint) in collusion with other brothers of the plaintiff by forging the signature of their mother sworn an affidavit on 29.12.1992 affirming the oral heba dated 17.09.1992 in favour of the said 3 sisters keeping the plaintiff in dark. Thereafter, the defendant No. 2-4 filed Title Suit No. 215 of 1996 in the Court of 1<sup>st</sup> Assistant Judge, Dhaka against the plaintiff and his brother, the defendant No.5 for evicting them from the suit property and by practicing fraud they obtained ex-parte judgment and decree on 23.06.1999. Against the said ex-parte judgment and decree dated 23.06.1999, the defendant No.1 of the said suit and the defendant No.5 of the present suit filed an application under Order IX, rule 13 of the Code of Civil Procedure for setting aside the said ex-parte decree whereupon Miscellaneous Case No. 4 of 2000 was started. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2(e).<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">     </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In the meantime after obtaining the ex-parte decree the plaintiffs of that suit filed Title Execution Case No. 4 of 2000 for evicting the defendants of the said suit. Thereafter, the defendant No.5 of the present suit filed an application in the Title Execution Case No.4 of 2000 for staying the proceeding of the title execution case till hearing of the Miscellaneous Case No. 4 of 2000, which was rejected on 30.10.2003. Against that order dated 30.10.2003 passed by the learned Assistant Judge, Narayangonj, the defendant No.5 of the present suit filed Civil Revision No. 4754 of 2006 before this Division. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2(f).<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">     </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Although, the defendant No. 2-4 of the present suit had no legal title and possession in the suit property, but they transferred the same along with ‘Kha’ scheduled property illigally in favour of the defendant No.1 vide registered sale deed No. 8864 dated 30.10.2005. The cause of action of the present suit arose when the defendant Nos. 2-4 evicted the plaintiff illegally from the suit property. Hence; the suit.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2(g).<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The petitioner as defendant No.1 entered appearance and contested the suit by filing an application under Order VII, Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure for rejection of plaint. Upon hearing of the said application for rejection of plaint, the court below rejected the same on 13.10.2009.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2(h).<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Being aggrieved by the said order dated 13.10.2009 passed by the learned Joint District Judge, Court No. 3, Dhaka in Title Suit No. 164 of 2007, the petitioner preferred this revisional application and obtained the present Rule.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. Syed Mokaddas Ali, the learned Advocate appearing for the petitioner submits that the plaintiff stated in the plaint about the ex-parte decree dated 23.06.1999 passed in Title Suit No. 127 of 1997 but with a malafide intention he has suppressed the fact that in Civil Revision No. 3834 of 2001 the High Court Division affirmed the said ex-parte decree dated 23.06.1999 which was further affirmed by the Appellate Division in C.P.L.A No. 1413 of 2002. He also submits that the ex-parte decree dated 23.06.1999 passed in Title Suit No. 127 of 1999 reached its finality when it was affirmed by the Appellate Division and hence the suit is barred by the doctrine of res-judicata and Mr. Mokaddas finally submits that the suit is barred by law in view of the facts that the judgment and decree passed in the earlier suit were affirmed by the Appellate Division as such the present suit cannot be maintainable. He referred some decisions namely Islami Bank Bangladesh Vs. Abdul Jalil reported in 53DLR(2001)-29 and Abdul Jalil and others Vs. Islami Bank reported in 53DLR(AD)(2001)-12.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. Moin Uddin alongwith Mr. Md. Kobad Hossain and Mr. Abul Hossain, the learned Advocates appearing for the opposite party No.1 by filing counter-affidavit submits that the matter relating to the application for rejection of plaint is the matter of evidence which may be proved by examination of witnesses on the dock and that the said matter do not come under the purview of Order VII Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure and as such the court below rightly rejected the application for rejection of plaint.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">He further submits that the court below did not commit any illegality or that the order passed by the court below does not suffer from any infirmity of law. He also submits that the summon-notices of the Title Suit No. 127 of 1997 were not served upon the defendants and against the ex-parte decree the defendant No.1 of the said suit as petitioner filed Miscellaneous Case No. 4 of 2000. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">He also submits that there was no decree in the said suit but on the strength of the decree the opposite party No.2-4 went to possession of the suit land and the present opposite party No.1 was dispossessed. He further submits that the name and character are different from each other and parties are also different, thus the present suit does not hit by resjudicata or any other law and as such the plaint of Title Suit No. 64 of 2007 does not come under the purview of Order VII Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure and he finally submits that the learned Court below rightly rejected the application for rejection of plaint and as such the present rule is liable to be discharged with cost.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In support of his submissions he referred some decisions namely Shahjahan Siraj (Md) Vs. Md. Rafique Quoraishi and others reported in 19 BLC (AD)-143,<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Abdul Jalil and others Vs. Islami Bank Bangladesh Ltd. and others reported in 64 DLR (AD) 107, Sreemati Pushpa Rani Das and another Vs. A.K.M. <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Habibur Rahman and others reported in 13 BLD</span> (AD)-217 and Md. Mahbubul Haque Vs. Md. A. Kader Monshi reported in 8 BLT (AD)-177.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">We have gone through the revisional application alongwith annexures therein and the counter-affidavit filed by the opposite party No.1. We have also considered the submissions made by the learned Advocates for the petitioner and the opposite party No.1.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Order VII rule 11 describes the procedure for rejection of plaint. It is necessary to quote Order VII rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure which runs as follows:- </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">“11. The plaint shall be rejected in the following cases:-</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 1in; text-indent: -0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">where it does not disclose a cause of action; </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 1in; text-indent: -0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">where the relief claimed is undervalued, and the plaintiff, on being required by the Court to correct the valuation within a time to be fixed by the Court fails to do so; </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 1in; text-indent: -0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(c)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">where the relief claimed is properly valued, but the plaint is written upon paper insufficiently stamped, and the plaintiff, on being required by the Court to supply the requisite stamp-paper within a time to be fixed by the Court, fails to do so; </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 1in; text-indent: -0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(d)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Where the suit appears from the statement in the plaint to be barred by any law. </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.75in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">[Provided that the time fixed by the Court for the correction of the valuation or supplying of the requisite stamp-paper shall not exceed twenty-one days]. </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.75in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">[(e) where any of the provisions of rule 9 (1A) is not complied with and the plaintiff on being required by the Court to comply therewith within a time to be fixed by the Court, fails to do so.] </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">On a plain reading of the aforesaid rule it is evident that the plaint shall be rejected on the grounds specified above. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For deciding an application under Order 7 Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure, the averments in the plaint need to be looked into.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The trial Court can exercise the power under Order 7 Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure at any stage of the suit before registering the plaint or after issuing summons to the defendants at any time before the conclusion of the trial.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For the purpose of deciding an application</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> under clauses (a) and (b) of Order 7 Rule 11 of the Code, the averments in the plaint are germane; the pleas taken by the defendants in <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the written statement would be wholly irrelevant.</span> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The basic question to be decided while dealing with an application filed under Order 7 Rule 11 of the Code is whether a real cause of action has been set out in the plaint. If on a meaningful and formal reading of the plaint, it appears to be manifestly fictitious and meritless in the sense of not disclosing a clear right to sue, the Court should exercise the power under Order 7 Rule 11 of the Code.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The real object of the Order 7 Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure is to keep out of Courts irresponsible suits.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>If it is found that the suit is an abuse of the process of the court in the sense that it is a bogus and irresponsible litigation, the jurisdiction under Order 7 Rule 11 of the Code can be exercised. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Question is whether a real cause of action has been set out in the plaint. Clever drafting creating illusions are not permitted in law and a clear right to sue should be shown in the plaint. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The Court should always be vigilant for scrutinizing the pleadings and materials placed before it to ascertain whether the litigation is frivolous or maintainable at all. The Court must exercise its powers at every stage in order to nip the frivolous cases in the bud.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">It is well settled now that a plaint may be rejected under Order 7 Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure merely on a plain reading of the plaint but in exceptional circumstances the Court may invoke it’s inherent jurisdiction and can through the plaint out in limine. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">It is also well settled that the plea of implied bar should ordinarily be decided on evidence, unless the facts disclosed in the pleading clearly prove that the suit is not maintainable. In exceptional cases recourse may be taken under section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In the case of Burmah Eastern Ltd. Vs. Burmah Eastern Employees Union reported in 18 DLR (Dhaka)-709 Mr. Justice Murshed held that apart from the question of Order 7 Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure, the Court can also exercise its inherent power in order to stop the harassment of the other party.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>Justice Murshed has held as follows;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">“The principles involved as twofold: in the first place, it contemplates that a still born suit should be properly buried, at its inception, so that no further time is consumed on a fruitless litigation. Secondly, it gives plaintiff a chance to retrace his steps, at the earliest possible moment, so that, if permissible under law, he may found a properly constituted case.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Order 7 Rule 11 of the Code, as quoted above enumerates certain categories under which the Court is called upon to reject a plaint, but, it is obvious that they are not exhaustive. It appears from the language of rule 11 of Order 7 that it requires that an incompetent suit should be laid at rest at the earliest moment so that no further time is wasted over what is bound to collapse as not being permitted by law.” </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In the case of Abdul Jalil and others Vs. Islamic Bank Bangladesh Ltd. and others reported in 53 DLR(AD)(2001)-12, it was held that;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">“ It is well settled that where a plaint cannot be rejected under Order rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure the court may invoke its inherent jurisdiction and reject the plaint taking recourse to section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure.” </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>It was further held that in the said case </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">“As the ultimate result of the suit is as clear as day light such a suit should be burried at its inception so that no further time is consumed in a fruitless litigation.” </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Coming to the case at hand, the defendants No. 2-4 after getting oral gift of their mother filed Title Suit No. 215 of 1996 in the Court of 1<sup>st</sup> Assistant Judge, Dhaka for declaration of title and recovery of khas possession of the suit property against the defendant No.5 of present suit making him defendant No.1 and making defendant No.2, the plaintiff of the present suit. Subsequently, the suit was renumbered as Title Suit No. 127 of 1997 in the Court of Assistant Judge, Nawabganj, Dhaka on transfer which was decreed ex-parte on 23.06.1999 in favour of the plaintiffs of the said suit declaring title of the suit property and also decreed for recovery of khas possession of the suit property. Against the aforesaid ex-parte decree, the plaintiff of the present suit as defendant No.2 filed an application under Order IX Rule 13 of the Code of Civil Procedure for setting aside the ex-parte decree dated 23.06.1999 of Title Suit No. 127 of 1997 whereupon the Miscellaneous Case No. 35 of 1999 was started. The petitioner of the aforesaid Miscellaneous Case that is, the plaintiff also filed Title Appeal No. 769 of 1999 in the Court of District Judge, Dhaka against the said ex-parte decree which was transferred to the Court of Subordinate Judge, Court No.3, Dhaka and after hearing the said appeal was allowed on 29.03.2001 setting aside the ex-parte decree and the suit was sent on remand to the trial court for hearing. Against the aforesaid judgment and order of the appellate court, the respondents of that appeal filed civil revision No. 3834 of 2001 before this Division and obtained Rule. After hearing the said Civil Revision No. 3834 of 2001 the Rule was made absolute on 28.02.2002 setting aside the judgment and decree of the appellate court and restored the ex-parte decree dated 23.06.1999 passed in Title Suit No. 127 of 1999. Against the judgment and order passed in Civil Revision No. 3834 of 2001 the present plaintiff filed Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 1413 of 2002 before the Appellate Division which was dismissed on 18.01.2003.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">    </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">We carefully scrutinized the plaints of both the suits as well as the judgments passed by the Court’s up to the Appellate Division. We are of the view that question which in the present plaint is now raising had already been considered and decided in the earlier suit once and for all and as such we hold that there was no cause of action for instituting the present suit. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The decree passed by the Appellate Division is the law of the land. Article 111 of our constitution provides that the law declared by the Appellate Division shall be binding on the High Court Division and the law declared by either Division of the Supreme Court shall be binding on all courts subordinate to it.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Since the judgment and decree passed by the earlier suit was affirmed by the Appellate Division the present suit cannot be maintainable in view of the fact that as the suit is barred by law and law declared by the Appellate Division in the judgment passed in Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 1413 of 2002.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">On the admitted facts appearing from the record itself, learned Advocate for the plaintiff-opposite parties were unable to show that all or any of this averments in the plaint disclose any cause of action giving rise to a triable issue. In our opinion, the trial court failed to perform it’s duty and overlooked this fatal defect.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Since the plaint suffers from this fatal defect, the continuance of such a suit tantamount to licensing a frivolous and vexatious litigation. This cannot be permitted as per law.</span></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">28.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.4pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In such a factual situation, in our considered</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> opinion, the court below has fallen into an error of law resulting in an error in his decision occasioning failure of justice in rejecting the application under Order 7 rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure and as such the impugned order is liable to be set aside. If the present suit is allowed to proceed further it would consume the time, energy and money of all the parties concerned. Therefore, this court <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">cannot allow such frivolous malafide proceedings</span> to continue. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">29.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In the result, the Rule is made absolute. <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">The judgment and order dated 13.10.2009 passed</span> by the learned Joint District Judge, Court No. 3,  Dhaka in Title Suit No. 164 of 2007 holding the suit to be maintainable is set aside and  the plaint is rejected under Order VII Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">30.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">There is no order as to costs. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">31.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.4pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Communicate this judgment and order at once.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">         Ed.  </span></strong></p><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___September__18/Issue%20__SEPTEMBER__18(2)__C.R.%2081%20of%2010___Md.%20Ashraful%20Kamal,%20J.__4.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Civil Revision No. 81 of 2010</span></strong></a></p></div></div></div></div>
666	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Habib Ahmed Shukur Morshed Vs.  Wakf Administrator &amp; ors., (Md. Ashraful Kamal, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Writ Petition No. 10733 of 2012   </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Moyeenul Islam Chowdhury, J And Md. Ashraful Kamal, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Md. Khalilur Rahman, Advocate with Mr. Hasan Mohammad Reyad, Advocate ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ  </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2014</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Habib Ahmed Shukur Morshed </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Wakf Administrator Bangladesh and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Waqfs Ordinance  </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-02</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(SPECIAL ORIGINAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; height: 277px; margin-right: auto;" width="658"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 294.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Moyeenul Islam Chowdhury, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">And</strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Md. Ashraful Kamal, J</strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> </strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">17.09.2014</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 55.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___September__18/Issue%20__SEPTEMBER__18(2)__W.%20P.%2010733%20of%2012__Md.%20Ashraful%20Kamal,%20J.____8.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 264.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Habib Ahmed Shukur Morshed</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">. . . Petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Wakf Administrator Bangladesh and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">... Respondents </span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Waqfs</span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> Ordinance (1 of 1962) </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Section 51</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">On a plain reading of the aforesaid section it is crystal clear that whenever any change needed in the management of an waqf’s property due to the death, retirement or removal of the mutawalli, the prospective mutawalli who is eligible or who considers himself to be eligible to succeed to the office of mutawalli in terms of the waqf deed shall forthwith notify such change to the Administrator of Waqfs. . . . (17)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Waqfs Ordinance (1 of 1962) </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 115%; text-align: justify;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Section 102</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 10pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">According to section 102 of the Waqfs Ordinance, 1962, no decision or order of the Administrator shall be questioned in any suit or other proceeding in any Court, except as otherwise expressly provided in the said Ordinance.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                         </span>. . .(19)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Waqfs Ordinance (1 of 1962) </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 115%; text-align: justify;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Section 43</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">It is important to understand the intention of the Wakif.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>In other words, the waqf-deed should be carried out in its totality and the waqf deed is the primary document for the procedure to be followed in the appointment of mutawalli. </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">This is to be noted that after the death of Waqif mutawalli, the present respondent No. 3 Humayun Morshed was appointed mutawalli on 04.01.1982, while he had been working abroad. Moreover, the Waqfs Administrator by his order dated 05.07.1994 appointed a Naib mutawalli to assist the Respondent No. 3 in administering the affairs of the Waqf Estate. This position was known to all including the present petitioner and the same was duly accepted by all the beneficiaries at that time. The respondent No. 3 had continued in his office as mutawalli for long 11 years till 1993.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>The respondent No. 3 has been residing in Bangladesh thus, he is neither incapable nor absent nor unwilling to hold the office of mutawalli and as such, there is no impediment in the present case. Thus, Section 43 of the Waqfs Ordinance does not have any manner of application in the present case. </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . .(25, 27 and 28)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 10pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">G. Nagewara Rao Vs. A.P.S.R.T Corpn (K. Subba Rao) 1959 AIR (SC) 306; 34 DLR (AD) 29; 48 DLR (AD) 10; 7 BLC (HC) 193; Showkat Ali Vs. Administrator of Waqfs, 29 DLR (SC) 276; 1995(1) All ER 315; R V. Crown Court and </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Amir Abdullah Khan Vs. Muhammad Attaullah Khan PLD 1990 (SC) 972 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Mr.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.4pt;"> Md.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.4pt;"> Khalilur Rahman, Advocate with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Mr. Hasan Mohammad Reyad, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">- - - For the petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Mahbubey Alam, Senior Advocate with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> Md.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> Ramzan Ali Sikder, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">- - - For the respondent No.3.</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Md. Ashraful Kamal, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">This Rule Nisi was issued calling upon the respondents to show cause as to why the order contained in Memo No. </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal;">JfËx/Qxcx/(4)2(2)</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> dated 02.08.2012 issued by the respondent No.2 removing the present mutawalli from the post of guardian mutawalliship and appointment of the respondent No.3 as mutawalli instead of the petitioner without giving any opportunity of being heard in accordance with law should not be declared to have been passed without lawful authority and is of no legal effect.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Brief facts, necessary for the disposal of this Rule, are as follows;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On 13.07.1976 Mr. Shukur Uddin Ahmmed of 59, Abdus Sattar Road, Rahmatgonj, Chittagong for charitable purpose as well as for the maintenance and support of his children and wife made a deed of waqf appointing himself as the first Mutwalli and shall continue till his death. According to the said waqf deed, after the death of the waqif, his son Md. Humayun Morshed will be the next mutawalli and in case of his (Md. Humayun Morshed) absence, incapacity, inability or unwillingness, provisions has been made in the waqf deed for appointment of mutawalli. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%;">After the death of the waqif Mr. Sukur Uddin Ahmed as first mutawalli, the respondent No.3 was appointed mutawalli of the waqf in question in accordance with the deed of waqf. After that, the proforma respondent No.5 (Mrs. Hasmot Ara Ahmed) applied before the Waqf Administrator for removal of the respondent No.3 from the post of mutawalli and to appoint her as guardian mutawalli. Upon consideration of the said application, the waqf administrator on 29.06.1993 appointed the proforma-respondent No.5 as guardian mutawalli of the said waqf property. Subsequently, upon an application filed by the respondent No.3, the waqf administrator by his order dated 05.07.1994 removed the proforma respondent No.5 (the guardian mutawalli) from the office and in her place appointed a Naib mutawalli nominated by the respondent No.3. Against the said order dated 05.07.1994, the proforma respondent No.5 filed a Writ Petition being No. 1733 of 1994, wherein the Rule issued was ultimately made absolute on 24.03.1998 and upheld by the Appellate Division on 30.04.2002.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">After that, the respondent No.3 on 10.12.2005 filed an application before the respondent No.1 for appointing him as mutawalli by removing the proforma respondent No.5 from the post of guardian mutwalli. At the same time, the petitioner also submitted an application before the waqf administrator for appointing him as mutawalli. After hearing the parties, the respondent No.1 (Waqf Administrator) rejected those applications on 02.07.2012 as the application were not filed as per<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>section 37 of the Waqfs Ordinance, 1962 and directed them to file fresh applications in accordance with law.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Thereafter, respondent No.3 and the petitioner filed applications on 07.07.2012 and on 12.07.2012 respectively complying with the condition as per section 37 of the Waqfs Ordinance, 1962. Upon receipt of those applications, the respondent No.1 directed the respondent No.4 to conduct an inquiry about the subject-matter. Accordingly, the respondent No.4 conducted the inquiry on 24.07.2012 and after completion of the inquiry, he submitted the report on 28.07.2012. In consideration of the recommendation of the report dated 28.07.2012, the respondent No.2 on 02.08.2012 removed the proforma respondent No. 5 from the post of mutawalli and<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>appointed the respondent No.3 as mutawalli.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Being aggrieved by the said order dated 02.08.2012 passed by the respondent No.2, appointing the respondent No.3 as mutawali, the petitioner preferred this Writ Petition and obtained the present Rule.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Md. Khalilur Rahman alongwith Mr. Hasan Mohammad Reyad, the learned Advocates appearing for the petitioner submits that the respondent No.2 without giving an opportunity of hearing to the petitioner passed the order dated 02.08.2012. He further submits that appointment of the respondent No.3 and removal of the proforma respondent No.5 was challenged on earlier occasion in Writ Petition No. 1733 of 1994 which was declared without lawful authority and of no legal effect vide judgment and order dated 24.03.1998 passed by the High Court Division and affirmed by the Appellate Division in Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 677 of 1998, but the respondent No.1 repeatedly passed the same order. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">      </span>He further submits that the inquiry officer without notifying the petitioner by issuing written notice conducted the alleged inquiry promptly on the very next day i.e. 24.07.2012 and made a report on 28.07.2012. He also submits that since the petitioner and respondent No.3 are contesting for the post of mutawalli in question as per waqf deed, therefore, the duty of the administrator of waqfs is to direct the contesting parties to go to the civil Court for the purpose of appointing the permanent mutawalli.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Rahman also submits that the respondent No.4 had conducted the enquiry in question by violating all norms of the inquiry for the purpose of depriving the petitioner of presenting his case. He further submits that the present petitioner is the only competent person to be appointed as mutawalli as per waqf deed since the respondent No.3 and other two elder brothers are permanently residing in the United States of America and Denmark and in view of the fact, the petitioner ought to have been appointed as mutawalli of the Waqf Estate in question. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Finally, Mr. Rahman submits that the Waqfs Administrator did not assign any reason about the non-consideration of the application of the petitioner, therefore, the very impugned order is a nonspeaking order and liable to be declared to have been passed without lawful authority and is of no legal effect.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In support of his submissions Mr. Rahman referred to the case of G. Nagewara Rao Vs. A.P.S.R.T Corpn (K. Subba Rao) reported in 1959 AIR(SC)-306, 34 DLR(AD) 29, 48DLR(AD)10, 7 BLC(HC) 193 and the case of Showkat Ali Vs. Administrator of Waqfs reported in 29 DLR(SC)276<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>and 1995(1) All ER, 315 in the case of R V. Crown Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Mahbubey Alam, the learned Senior Advocate along with the learned Advocate Mr. Ramzan Ali Sikder appearing for the respondent No.3<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>at first submits that the facts and circumstances of the present case are different from those in the writ petition No. 1733 of 1994 and Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 677 of 1998 because the High Court Division set aside the order dated 05.07.1994 on the basis that the proforma respondent No.5 had not been given any opportunity to be heard as required under section 32 of the Waqf Ordinance, 1962. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He further submits that the inquiry officer after observing all the formalities according to the law and upon hearing both the parties on 25.07.2012 at the office of the Waqfs Administrator made his report. So the inquiry process was done thoroughly in compliance with the relevance provision of law and as such the writ petition is misleading, misconceived and the Rule is liable to be discharged as being not maintainable.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">We have gone through the writ petition along with annexures therein, affidavit-in-opposition along with annexures therein and considered the submissions made by the respective parties. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Firstly, we have carefully examined the judgment and order passed in Writ Petition No. 1733 of 1994 and Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 677 of 1995. After examination, it is crystal clear that Writ Petition No. 1733 of 1994 and Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 677 of 1995 are absolutely different from the instant case and has no manner of the application in the present Writ Petition.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin-left: 0in; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Next, it is necessary to quote section 51 of the Waqfs Ordinance which runs as thus;</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin-left: 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“ Notification of Changes in Enrolled Waqfs-(1) In the case of any change in the management of an enrolled waqf due to the death, retirement or removal of the mutawalli, the prospective mutawalli who is eligible or who considers himself to be eligible to succeed to the office of mutawalli in terms of the waqf deed or according to the custom or usage of the waqf, shall forthwith, and any other person may, notify the change to the Administrator.</span></em></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">(2) In the case of any other change in any of the particulars mentioned in section 47, the mutawalli shall, within six months from the occurrence of the change, notify such change to the Administrator.”</span></em></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On a plain reading of the aforesaid section it is crystal clear that whenever any change needed in the management of an waqf’s property due to the death, retirement or removal of the mutawalli, the prospective mutawalli who is eligible or who considers himself to be eligible to succeed to the office of mutawalli in terms of the waqf deed shall forthwith notify such change to the Administrator of Waqfs.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the present case, the petitioner as a prospective mutawalli, who is allegedly eligible and considers himself to be eligible to succeed to the office of the mutawalli in question as per waqf deed notified the Administrator as per section 51 of the Waqfs Ordinance. But the Waqfs Administrator rejected the same and appointed respondent No.3 as mutawalli.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">The Waqfs Ordinance being a special statute</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> provides a special procedure to be followed. And according to section 102 of the Waqfs Ordinance, 1962, no decision or order of the Administrator shall be questioned in any suit or <span style="letter-spacing: -.5pt;">other proceeding in any Court, except as otherwise</span> expressly provided in the said Ordinance.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The one and only core ground taken by the writ petitioner is that the inquiry officer (respondent No.4) without notifying the petitioner conducted the alleged inquiry promptly and on the basis of the said report the respondent No.2 passed the impugned order dated 02.08.2012 which is a clear violation of the principle of natural justice. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On a keen perusal of the record it appears that the respondent No. 4 duly conducted the investigation and submitted its Report dated 28.07.2012 to the respondent No. 1. Moreover, inquiry was carried out upon notifying the parties including the writ petitioner and also upon observing all formalities. Based on the aforesaid Inquiry Report and considering the submissions made by the parties on 25.07.2012 at the office of the Waqfs Administrator and examining the relevant documents, the respondent No. 2 appointed the respondent No. 3 as mutawalli. Therefore, the allegation of not affording any opportunity of being heard has no legs to stand upon. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It is necessary to quote the pertinent portion of the report dated 28.07.2012 which has been concluded as under; </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;
