line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal;">Bfe¡l A¢g­pl ü¡lL ew JxfËx/QVx (cx)/30 a¡w 23/07/2012Cw f­œl ¢e­cÑnœ²­j f§­hÑ AhNa Ll¡Cu¡ Na 24/07/2012Cw a¡¢l­M p­lS¢j­e Ef¢ÙÛa qCu¡ ac¿¹ L¡S L¢lz E­õMÉ ®k, ac¿¹ L¡­m c¤CSe clM¡Ù¹L¡l£l HLSeJ Ef¢ÙÛa ¢R­me e¡z Ju¡Lg H­ø­Vl h¡s£­a hph¡pL¡l£ ®m¡LSe Ef¢ÙÛa ¢R­mez a¡l¡ S¡e¡e clM¡Ù¹L¡l£ c¤CSeC Y¡L¡u B­Re Hhw haÑj¡e A¢ii¡hL ®j¡a¡Ju¡õ£ h¡wm¡­c­n e¡Cz ac¿¹ Ll¡l fl ¢ce clM¡Ù¹L¡l£ c¤C SeC ¢e­jÀ ü¡rlL¡l£l A¢g­p Ef¢ÙÛa qe Hhw ¢eS ¢eS hš²hÉ ®ce Hhw ¢eS ¢eS clM¡­Ù¹l üf­r k¤¢š² J BCeNa pjbÑe ­cM¡­e¡l ®Qø¡ L­lez</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">” </span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On a plain reading of the aforesaid portion of the report it transpires that the inquiry was carried out by not only notifying the parties including the writ petitioner and also upon observing all formalities. So the allegation of not affording any opportunity to the petitioner of being heard is not sustainable at all.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">For implication and legal position of the referential order dated 02.08.2012, it is necessary to quote the pertinent portion of the Amir Abdullah Khan –Vs- Muhammad Attaullah Khan reported in PLD 1990 (SC) 972 wherein the Hon’ble Supreme Court of Pakistan held as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">“<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">17. Contents or part of the contents of another document may be incorporated by reference, and in such cases the other document, so far as it is incorporated, is read with the document under consideration.”</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Since the impugned order dated 02.08.2012 was passed by making reference to and based on the inquiry report dated 28.07.2012, therefore, the said inquiry report should be read together with the impugned order dated 02.08.2012 as a referential order to understand the reason for appointment of the respondent No. 3 as mutawalli. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">It is important to understand the intention of the Wakif.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>In other words, the waqf-deed should be carried out in its totality and the waqf deed is the primary document for the procedure to be followed in the appointment of mutawalli. Therefore, it is necessary to quote the Clause 1 and 2 of the Waqf-deed dated 13.07.1976, which runs thus:- </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">“(1) I appoint myself the first trusty for mutwali of this work during the time of my natural life and waqf shall all alone belong as the waqf state Shukur Uddin Ahmed son of late Amir Hossain of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>59 Abdus Sattar Road, Rahmatgonj, Chittagong aged <span style="color: #000000;">about 73 years by cash Sunni Muslim and by profession an </span>Advocate Judge Court Chittagong<span style="color: #000000;">.”</span></span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Clause (2) after my death or retirement,</span></em><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> my son Md. Humayun Morshed <u>shall be the second mutwalli</u> of the waqf and if necessary, he will have the right to appoint of Naib Mutwalli for the </span></em><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.1pt;">management of waqf properties and for </span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">carrying on the administrative duties of the Mutwalli for him and his behalf.”</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">26.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">On a plain reading of the aforesaid clause 1 and 2 of the Waqf Deed it is crystal clear that after the natural death of the Waqif mutawalli, the respondent No. 3 is the designated mutawalli of the Waqf Estate. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">27.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">This is to be noted that after the death of Waqif mutawalli, the present respondent No. 3 Humayun Morshed was appointed mutawalli on 04.01.1982, while he had been working abroad. Moreover, the Waqfs Administrator by his order dated 05.07.1994 appointed a Naib mutawalli to assist the Respondent No. 3 in administering the affairs of the Waqf Estate. This position was known to all including the present petitioner and the same was duly accepted by all the beneficiaries at that time. The respondent No. 3 had continued in his office as mutawalli for long 11 years till 1993.  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">28.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">The respondent No. 3 has been residing in Bangladesh thus, he is neither incapable nor absent nor unwilling to hold the office of mutawalli and as such, there is no impediment in the present case. Thus, Section 43 of the Waqfs Ordinance does not have any manner of application in the present case.  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">29.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">In the light of the above facts and circumstances, we find no substances in this writ petition. All the allegations made by the petitioner in its petition are amorphous, fallacious and absolutely based on erroneous notion. Accordingly, the Rule is liable to be discharged. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">30.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt;">In the result, the Rule is discharged without any order as to cost.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">31.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">                </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">Communicate the judgment and order at once.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 9.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: red;"><span style="color: #000000;">Ed. </span></span></strong></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___September__18/Issue%20__SEPTEMBER__18(2)__W.%20P.%2010733%20of%2012__Md.%20Ashraful%20Kamal,%20J.____8.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Writ Petition No. </span></strong></a><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">10733 of 2012 </span></strong></p></div></div></div></div>

Accordingly, here as well this Court finds itself deciding against the Petitioners’ standing in judicial review in the present circumstances.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                    </span>. . .(28)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Article 117</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Administrative Tribunal Act (VII of 1981)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 2AA</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">The ICB established under the Investment Corporation Bangladesh Ordinance, 1976 is deemed to be a statutory public authority for the purposes of the Act and by which reason the Petitioners’ grievances, if any, arising out of terms and conditions of their service fall to be squarely governed by the </span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Tribunal established under the Administrative</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> Tribunal Act.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                     </span>. . . (29)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Article 117</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It is deemed prudent at this juncture to enumerate the points decided by the Appellate Division touching upon the authority of this Court <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">vis-à-vis</em> Article 117 of the Constitution: </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">1) Any person in the service of Republic or any statutory authority cannot seek judicial review in respect of terms and conditions of service or action taken relating to him as a person to such service including transfer, promotion, and pension rights, except: </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-indent: -0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">in matters relating to challenging the vires of the law;</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-indent: -0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">infringement of fundamental rights in which case also, there must be sufficient pleadings of such violation keeping in mind that such plea also can be taken in the tribunal because the constitution being the supreme law of the Country, it can be taken in aid by any Court/tribunal.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">2) The Administrative Tribunal shall be competent to deal with those matters and in appropriate cases of emergency, it can also pass interim order of injunction/stay subject to compliance of certain formalities.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">3) The views taken in Mujibur Rahman case 44 DLR (AD) 111 have been overruled. </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">4) If the action of the authority or order complained of in relation to the above matters are found to be in coram non judice or without jurisdiction or is found malafide, judicial review is not available and the administrative tribunal can deal with these issues also. . . . (30)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 105%; text-align: justify;"><strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 105%;">Ajay Hasia Vs. Capt. K.C. N. Chandrasekharan &amp; Another, AIR (1998)SC 795;</span></em></strong> <strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 105%;">Mehmood Alam Tariq and Ors. Vs. State of Rajasthan Ors., MANU/SC/0278/1988;</span></em></strong> <strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 105%;">Madhya Pradesh Public Service Commission Vs. State of Punjab and ors, AIR (2001) SC 152;</span></em></strong> <strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 105%;">A. (2008) 5 </span></em></strong><strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">SCC 416;</span></em></strong> <strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">Chandra Prakash Tiwari Vs. Shakuntala</span></em></strong><strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 105%;"> Shukla MANU/SC/0447/2002: (2002) 6 SCC 127; Manish Kumar Shah Vs. F. Hassan Ariff, Senior Advocate</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Fida M. Kamal, Senior Advocate, </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Mr. S.M. Atikur Rahman, Advocate and</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> Md.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> Zafar Ali Khan, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">- - -<u>For the Petitioner</u> </span></em></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">(In both Writ Petitions).</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">Dr. Shahdeen Malik, Senior Advocate with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Monzur Alam, Advocate and</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">- - - <u>For the Respondent Nos. 6-9</u></span></em></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">(In Writ Petition No. 14424 of 2016)</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. S.M. Moniruzzaman, Advocate<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . . <u>For the Respondent No. 5</u> </span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">(In Writ Petition No. 15283 of 2016)</span></em></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoHeading9" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 24pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal;">Syed Refaat Ahmed, J:</span></u></strong><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal;"> These are two Applications predicated on similar facts that have given rise to two Rules Nisi requiring consideration of common core issues of law, thereby, justifying both Rules Nisi to be disposed of by this single Judgment. The initial point of reference in this regard has to be common parallel directions of the Hon’ble </span><span style="mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Chief Justice of 7.3.2017 requiring this particular</span><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal;"> Bench to hear and dispose of each matter.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In each of the Writ Petition Nos. 14424 and 15283 of 2016 a Rule Nisi was similarly issued calling upon the Respondents to show cause as to why Rule 9(4) of the </span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal;">Ce­iØV­j¾V L­f¡Ñ­lne Ah h¡wm¡­cn Hl Ef-hÉhØq¡fe¡ f¢lQ¡mL J jq¡hÉhØq¡fL Hhw Eq¡l Ad£eØq ®L¡Çf¡¢el fËd¡e ¢eh¡Ñq£ LjÑLa¡Ñ ¢e­u¡N ¢h¢dj¡m¡, 2016</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> or Rules for the Appointment of Deputy Managing Director and General Manager of Investment Corporation of Bangladesh and Chief Executive Officer of its Affiliated Companies, 2016 (“Rules”) (Annexure-‘A’) as published in the Official Gazette dated 1.6.2016 as being arbitrary and unreasonable as a delegated legislation should not be declared <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">ultra virus</em> to the Constitution and why the Memo No. 53.00.0000.422.12.001.16-17 dated 7.11.2016 issued by the Respondent No. 3 (Annexure-‘B’) giving promotion to 9 officers to the rank of Deputy General Manager/Equivalent posts of the Investment Corporation of Bangladesh (ICB) as General Manager excluding the Petitioner should not be declared to have been issued without lawful authority and of no legal effect and/or pass such other or further Order or Orders as to this Court may seem fit and proper. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In Writ Petition No. 14424 of 2016 the facts concern the Petitioner who after joining ICB has had a successful career since. She was promoted to the post of Principal Officer on 18.10.1994 and as Senior Principal Officer on 1.11.1998. Subsequently, the Petitioner was promoted to the Post of Assistant General Manager (AGM) on 23.4.2007 and on the basis of her satisfactory performance to the Department, she was promoted to the post of <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Deputy General Manager (DGM) on 29.12.2011.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Government promulgated the Rules under the power vested in Section 13 of the Investment Corporation of Bangladesh Act, 2014. It is stated that the Rules provide for appointment of General Manager by way of promotion. Schedule 2 of the Rules provides<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>that the Selection Committee shall give marks to candidates for promotion out of 85 which shall include 50 marks for the Annual Credential Report (ACR), 15 marks for Educational Qualification, 10 marks for Professional Qualifications and 15 marks for Service Experience. Part 2 of Schedule 2 provides for 15 marks for interview.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Petitioner obtained 78.50 marks out of 85 by the Selection Committee and stood 8<sup>th</sup>. However, she was given 8 marks out of 15 by the Interview Committee (9 being the pass mark as 60% of 15) and was not included in the Panel of Candidates sent to the Government for Promotion.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It is asserted that the Respondents have resorted to assigning marks of their own sweet will and choice to their chosen candidates and promoted Serial Nos. 16, 19 and 20 in preference to the Petitioner from the Merit List prepared by the Selection Committee marking the entire selection process redundant.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It is submitted against such factual backdrop that the provision for 15 marks in interview, assigning 60% as pass mark in the interview and preparation of the Final Panel for promotion are arbitrary and unreasonable since the same have given the option to the Respondents to pick and choose illegally and deprive the more competent candidate to be promoted to the post of General Manager.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In Writ Petition No. 15283 of 2016 filed on similar facts and grounds, the bare facts for disposal are that upon entering ICB’s service in 1987 the Petitioner has successfully moved up the ranks as evident in his promotion to the post of Principal Officer on 18.10.1994 and as Senior Principal Officer on 1.11.2018. Subsequently, the Petitioner was promoted to the post of AGM on 23.4.2007 and on the basis of his satisfactory performance to the Department, he was promoted to the post of DGM on 29.12.2011.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Petitioner in this case obtained 82 marks out of 85 by the Selection Committee and stood 2<sup>nd</sup>. However, he was given 8 marks out of 15 by the Interview Committee (9 being the pass mark as 60% of 15) and was not even included in the Panel of Candidates sent to the Government for promotion. Here as well, it is contended that the Respondents have taken the advantage of giving marks of their own sweet will and choice to their chosen candidates and promoted Respondent Nos. 7 to 11 and Serial Nos. 16, 19 and 20 from the Merit List prepared by the Selection Committee making the entire Selection Process farcical redundant.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In enunciating the grounds behind the prayers for issuance of the Rules Nisi the learned Advocate for the Petitioners in both Writ Petitions Mr. A.F. Hassan Ariff has dealt at length on the schematic structure of the Rules. He has, accordingly, deconstructed the provisions of Rule 9, the interrelationship between Rule 6 and 9 and how the Petitioners in both Writ Petitions perceive their substantive effect in terms of Schedule 2 as draws on Rules 6(2) and 9(1). Rules 6 and 9 are, accordingly, reproduced hereinbelow for ease of reference: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;
