text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . Petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> Amzad Hossain and 6 (six) others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . .Opposite-Parties</span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.25pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Code</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;">Section 494</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Court is required to exercise its function judiciously to accord withdrawal of any accused from the prosecution. In other words, the consent should not be given mechanically for the purpose of withdrawal of a criminal case particularly a murder case like present one. . . . (13)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 494</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Additional Sessions Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Naogaon without giving any reason, just on taking into consideration of the Memo issued by the Ministry of Home Affairs, mechanically allowed the same as like as a routine work and accorded permission for non-prosecution which is neither sustainable in law nor maintainable on the face of the given case.               . . .(14)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 494</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">It is to be notable here that the Public Prosecutor should assist the Court in accordance with law and should have acted lawfully but in the instant case, we find that the Public Prosecutor failed to perform his legal duties in accordance with law which is deprecated by all fair means.    . . .(15)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Syed Matiur Rahman @ Motiur Rahman @ Makhan Vs. The State 1984 BLD (AD) 261; Prativa Rani Dey (Tirtha) Vs. Dr. Mohammad Yousuf, Chittagong Medical College and others 52 DLR (AD) 8; Shah Obaidul Mannan and another Vs. The State and another 8 BLT (AD) 42 and Md. Hafiz Uddin Vs. The State and others 20 BLT (HCD) 245 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Mr. Ashif Hasan Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . . For the petitioner.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Mrs. Anwara Shahjahan, DAG with </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Mr. Kazi Bashir Ahmed, AAG</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.5pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.5pt; mso-font-width: 95%;">. . . For the  Respondents </span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mohammad Ullah, J:</span></u></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> On an application under section 561A of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898, Rule was issued calling upon the opposite parties to show cause as to why the impugned orders dated 05.11.2003 and 26.05.2004 passed by the Additional Sessions Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Naogaon allowing the prayer filed by the Public Prosecutor, Naogaon for withdrawal of the case pursuant to letters of the Ministry of Home Affair in Session Case No. 45 of 1997 should not be quashed and/or why such other or further order or orders should not be passed as to this Court may seem fit and proper.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">2.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">At the time of issuance of the Rule dated 26.10.2005, all further proceedings of Session Case No. 45 of 1997 was stayed initially for a period of 3 (three) months and from time to time the period of stay was extended and lastly on 17.11.2009 the same was extended till disposal of the Rule.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">3.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The facts relevant for disposal of the Rule, are that, one Md. Khandakar Mustafa lodged a First Information Report (FIR) on 11.12.1995 about the killing of his nephew with Naogaon Police Station alleging, <em>inter alia</em>, that on 10.12.1995 at about 5.30 pm the nephew of the informant Khandakar Abdullah Al-Masud Sumon  (Sumon) went to Paharpur Seven Star Club for a discussion about obscuring Independent Day of the country and he along with some others, after their discussions, went to the house of one Mostakim Hossain to bring a harmonium. Having not got the harmonium at about 6.00pm they were returning back to the club but on the way back when they reached near the house of one Harun Master located at the Badal Gasi Road the FIR named accused persons being with armed, hokey-stick, lathi and others dangerous weapons encircled  them and the accused Kazi Salim Uddin ordered to the other accused persons to kill the victim Sumon and then and there the accused Afzal Hossain inflicted hokey-stick blow on the head of Sumon causing serious bleeding injury who felt on the ground and at that time the accused Babu and Amzad dealt hokey-stick and lathi blow on Sumon causing serious injury on left eye and forehead and other accused persons indiscriminately beaten on the different  parts of body of Sumon with hokey-stick and lathi and having heard the hue and cry of Sumon some local people rushed to the place of occurrence and hurriedly the accused persons fled away. The local people took Sumon at Naogan General Hospital for treatment and on the following day on 11.12.1995 at about 10.15 a.m. the victim Sumon succumbed therein. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">4.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Accordingly, Naogaon Police Station Case No. 12 dated 11.12.1995 was recorded against 12 (twelve) accused persons under sections 302, 34 and 201 of the Penal Code including the accused-opposite-parties No. 1-4. After investigation police submitted charge sheet on 05.10.1996 against 12 (twelve) accused persons including the accused-opposite-parties No. 1-4 under sections 302, 34 and 201 of the Penal Code.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">5.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Thereafter the case record has been transferred to the learned Sessions Judge for trial wherein it was registered as Session Case No. 45 of 1997. The learned Sessions Judge transmitted the case record to the Additional Sessions Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Naogaon for trial and disposal. Subsequently the charge was framed against all the 12 (twelve) accused persons including the accused-opposite-parties No. 1-4 under sections 302, 34 and 201 of the Penal Code. The prosecution produced two PWs including the petitioner in support of its case wherein some of the accused persons cross-examined them (PWs 1 &amp; 2) and accused-opposite-parties No. 1 and 2 could not cross-examine those PWs since they were absconding at the relevant time. It has been stated in the petition that the accused-opposite-parties No. 1 and 2 Md. Afzal Hossain and Amzad Hossain granted ad-interim bail by this Court but subsequently the said Rule was discharged and their ad-interim bail was cancelled and since then they are absconding.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">6.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Pursuant to a letter issued by the Ministry of Home Affairs, the Public Prosecutor filed an application under section 494 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898 (“the Code, 1898”) for withdrawal from the prosecution of the accused-opposite-parties No. 1 and 2 (Md. Afzal Hossain and Amzad Hossain) before the trial Court who upon hearing the Public Prosecutor and on consideration of the materials on record by order dated 22.03.2003 rejected the same. The Ministry of Home Affairs issued another letter for withdrawal of another co-accused Kazi Salim Uddin from the prosecution and accordingly the Public Prosecutor filed further application under section 494 of the Code on behalf of the accused Kazi Salim Uddin, Md. Afzal Hossain and Amzad Hossain for withdrawal from the prosecution and the learned Additional Sessions Judge allowed the same by order dated 05.11.2003. Subsequently the Public Prosecutor filed another application for withdrawal of the co-accused Babu from the prosecution under the same section pursuant to a decision of the Ministry of Home Affairs. Wherein the learned Additional Sessions Judge by order dated 26.05.2004 allowed the same.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">7.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the aforesaid two impugned decisions of the Additional Sessions Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Naogaon, the petitioner being the father of the deceased Sumon moved this Court and obtained the Rule. It has also been stated in the petition that the informant of the case in the meantime died on 02.12.2002.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">8.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. Ashif Hasan, learned Advocate appearing for the petitioner in support of the Rule submits that the learned Additional Sessions Judge did not at all look into the gravity of the offence of the accused-opposite-parties No. 1-4 as disclosed in the FIR and charge-sheet; moreover in the meantime two prosecution witnesses have been examined and even the learned Court did not take into consideration that the accused-opposite-parties No. 1 and 2 were very much absconding when they were discharged for the prosecution and hence the impugned orders are ex-facie illegal and not tenable in law and as such those are liable to be interfered by this Court for securing ends of justice. Having drawn the attention of this Court to the impugned orders, the learned Advocate submits further that the learned Additional Sessions Judge without applying the judicial mind mechanically passed the impugned order while on the self-same matter earlier on 22.03.2003 on the safe-same application the same Court accurately assigning irrefutable reasonings rejected the application for withdrawal filed by the Public Prosecutor on behalf of the accused-opposite-parties No. 1 and 2. Over and again the learned Additional Sessions Judge cannot sit over of its own decision and pass the impugned orders and as such the impugned decisions are liable to be set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">9.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The learned Advocate in support of his contentions has referred to the decisions in the cases of- </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">(1)<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Syed Matiur Rahman @ Motiur Rahman @ Makhan Vs. The State reported in 1984 BLD (AD)261; </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">(2)<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Prativa Rani Dey (Tirtha) Vs. Dr. Mohammad Yousuf, Chittagong Medical College and others reported in 52 DLR(AD)8</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">(3)<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Shah Obaidul Mannan and another Vs. The State and another reported in 8 BLT (AD)42 and </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">(4)<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Md. Hafiz Uddin Vs. The State and others reported in 20BLT(HCD)245.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">10.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">No one appears on behalf of the accused-opposite-parties No. 1-4 when the matter is taken up for hearing.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">11.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">We have heard the submissions of the learned Assistant Attorney General who has adopted the submissions as advanced by the learned Advocate for the petitioner and he adds that the Public Prosecutor who filed the application for withdrawal from the prosecution should be brought under law since he filed application for withdrawal in a plain and simple murder case with an ulterior motive.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">12.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Heard the learned Advocates, perused the materials on record placed before us including the impugned orders passed by the learned Additional Sessions Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Naogaon. Section 494 of the Code, 1898 has given power to the learned Public Prosecutor to file application for withdraw any case from the prosecution but that sort of decision should be taken by the Court concern judiciously. The consent mentioned in section 494 of the Code, 1898 is not to be given mechanically rather the Court is to exercise its judicial authority before giving such consent which implies that the Court will have to examine the materials on which the Government decides withdrawal of the case. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">13.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">It appears that the accused-opposite-parties No. 1 and 2 were absconding when the decision of withdrawal was passed. But a long standing practice and decision of the Apex Court that withdrawal from prosecution is subject to consent by the trial Judge and when the accused person or persons is/are absconding the discretion should not to be exercised in favour of such absconding person(s). It also appears from the materials on record that there is a direct and specific allegation against the accused-opposite-parties No. 1-4 for the commission of offence under sections 302, 34 and 201 of the Penal Code to kill the victim Sumon and upon such allegations police report has been submitted into the matter, the charge against the opposite-parties No. 1-4 and other accused persons have been framed and meanwhile two PWs were examined including the informant. From the impugned orders passed by the learned Additional Sessions Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Naogaon it appears that in fact no reasons or grounds has been assigned for the withdrawal of the case from the prosecution and there is no indication that what materials were considered before taking such decisions. Although the concerned Judge assigning the cogent reasons earlier application for withdrawal from the prosecution rejected on 22.03.2003 filed on behalf of the accused-opposite-parties No. 1 and 2 Md. Afzal Hossain and Amzad Hossain. The learned Additional Sessions Judge by order dated 22.03.2003 while rejecting the application filed by the Public Prosecutor for withdrawal from the prosecution of the accused Md. Afzal Hossain and Amzad Hossain assigned the reason to the effect that “this is not a political case rather it is a pure and simple murder”. But subsequently the self-same Court while taking decisions in favour of the withdrawal from prosecution did not assign any reason we therefore thought that for not giving any ground, the reason best known to him. The present facts and circumstances of the case, let us consider whether on the basis of the decisions of the Government a case can be allowed to be withdrawn.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">14.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">It appears from the impugned decisions of withdrawal from the prosecution the learned Additional Sessions Judge did not apply its judicial mind at all while taking the impugned decisions of withdrawal from the prosecution of the accused-opposite-parties No. 1-4. It is now well-settled that the Court is required to exercise its function judiciously to accord withdrawal of any accused from the prosecution. In other words, the consent should not be given mechanically for the purpose of withdrawal of a criminal case particularly a murder case like present one. In support of the view taken by us, we may refer to the decision in the case of Prativa Rani Dey (Tirtha) Vs. Dr. Mohammad Yousuf, Chittagong Medical College and others reported in 52 DLR (AD) 8 wherein their lordships observed that:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">“It further appears that the accused persons in this case are all along absconding. And while they are still absconding the Government decided to withdraw from the prosecution which was allowed. It is now well settled that such withdrawals subject to consent by the trial Judge and when the accused persons are still absconding the discretion ought not to have been exercised by the Divisional Special Judge in the present case.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">It is well settled that the consent mentioned in section 494 of the Code of Criminal Procedure is not to be given mechanically. The Court is to exercise its function judicially before giving such consent which implies that the Court will have to examine the materials on which the Government decides withdrawal of a case.”</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">15.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In the facts and circumstances of the instant case, it appears that the learned Additional Sessions Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Naogaon without giving any reason, just on taking into consideration of the Memo issued by the Ministry of Home Affairs, mechanically allowed the same as like as a routine work and accorded permission for non-prosecution which is neither sustainable in law nor maintainable on the face of the given case.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">16.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">It is to be notable here that the Public Prosecutor should assist the Court in accordance with law and should have acted lawfully but in the instant case, we find that the Public Prosecutor failed to perform his legal duties in accordance with law which is deprecated by all fair means.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">17.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In view of what have been stated above and in the facts and circumstances of the case, we find merit in the Rule. Accordingly, the Rule is made absolute. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">18.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The impugned orders dated 05.11.2003 and 26.05.2004 passed by the learned Additional Sessions Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Naogaon in Session Case No. 45 of 1997 is hereby set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">19.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Since the matter is old and the FIR was lodged in the year, 1995, we consider it prudent to direct the Court concern to conclude the trial of the Session Case No. 45 of 1997 with utmost expedition preferably within 6 (six) months from the date of receipt of this order without any fail. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.5pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">20.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The order of stay is hereby recalled and vacated.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.5pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">21.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Garamond; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Send a copy of the judgment and order to the Court concerned at once.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">         Ed. </span></strong></p><p> </p><div><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___September__18/Issue%20__SEPTEMBER_18(2)__Crl.%20Misc.%2013400%20of%2005__Mohammad%20Ullah,%20J__2.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" title=""><strong><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. </span></strong></a><strong><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">13400 of 2005</span></strong></p></div></div></div></div>
672	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Monjur Morshed Khan and others Vs. ACC and another, (Hasan Foez Siddique, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CRIMINAL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL NO.164 OF 2017  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Syed Mahmud Hossain, CJ,  Muhammad Imman Ali, J, Hasan Foez Siddique, J Mirza Hussain Haider, J. </p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Rokanuddin Mahmud, Senior Advocate, instructed by Bivash Chandra Biswas, Advocate-on-Record. ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ (AD)     </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Monjur Morshed Khan and others </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Durntiy Daman Commission (Anti Corruption Commission) and another </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Code of Criminal Procedure  </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-02</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">APPELLATE DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(CRIMINAL</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; height: 188px;" width="660"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes; height: 112.85pt;"><td style="width: 270.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Syed Mahmud Hossain, CJ, </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Muhammad Imman Ali, J,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Hasan Foez Siddique, J</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mirza Hussain Haider, J. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">08.03.2018</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 46.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___September__18/Issue__SEPTEMBER_%2018(2)__Crl.%20P.%20164%20of%2017__Hasan%20Foez%20Siddique__AD__2.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Monjur Morshed Khan and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Petitioners</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">-Versus</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Durntiy Daman Commission (Anti Corruption Commission) and another</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Respondents</span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Sections 156 and 173(3B)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 105%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"><span style="color: #000000;">The provision of further investigation is</span> comprehended under section 173 (3B) of the Code of Criminal Procedure is something which is the exclusive prerogative of the investigation agencies. The provision does not, in specific terms, mention about any power of the Court to order further investigation. Section 156 of the Code of Criminal Procedure uses the expression ‘investigation’ only and not ‘further investigation’. No doubt, where there is already an investigation culminating in a police report, the court can trigger into motion the power of the police to conduct further investigation under section 173(3B) of the Code of Criminal Procedure. The said provision does not provide any specific provision that in order to hold further investigation by the police, it is necessary to take permission of the Court.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>. . .(9)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 173</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 107%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The discharge of the accused on the basis of the final report does not amount to acquittal and so there is no bar of holding further investigation even after acceptance of police report when fresh material comes to light against accused persons. The investigating agency cannot keep quiet. The words, ‘nothing is this section shall be deemed to preclude further investigation’ used in section 173(3B) clearly emphasize that nothing in Section 173 shall be construed to preclude further investigation by the investigating agency in respect of an offence after a report under section 173(1) of the Code. The Court can order for further investigation even after acceptance of final report stating non-availability of the materials. Since the order of discharge neither amounts to an acquittal nor to a final order, the accused can be proceeded against for the same offence on the basis of supplementary report submitted on holding further investigation or on the basis of naraji petition filed by the informant/ complainant. It is no longer res integra that the Court, if exigent to do so, to espouse the </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">cause of justice, can trigger further investigation</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> even after a final report is submitted under section 173(3B) of the Code.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">       </span>. . .(12)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Sections 154 to 173</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The investigation of crime is carried out dehors the mandate contained in the Code of Criminal Procedure containing sections 154-173 of the Code and that the further investigation is a statutory right of the investigating agency under section 173(3B). The High Court Division rightly allowed the investigating agency of holding further investigation even after submission of the police report and after acceptance of the same.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">     </span>. . .(13)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Abdur Rahman Vs. State 29 DLR (SC) 256 and Dr. H.B.M. Iqbal Vs. the State 12 MLR (AD) 30 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For the Petitioner:</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mr. Rokanuddin Mahmud, Senior Advocate, instructed by Bivash Chandra Biswas, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For Respondent:</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mr. Khurshid Alam Khan, Advocate, instructed by <span style="letter-spacing: -.5pt;">Mr. Md. Zahirul Islam, Advocate</span>-on-on Record.</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">Hasan Foez Siddique, J</span></u></strong><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The delay in filing this petition is condoned.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">This criminal petition for leave to appeal is directed against the judgment and order dated 09.11.2016 passed by the High Court Division in Criminal Revision No.1062 of 2016 disposing of the Rule.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The relevant facts, for the disposal of this <span style="letter-spacing: -.5pt;">petition, are that on 31.12.2013 Md. Moniruzzaman</span> Khan, Deputy Director, Durnity Daman Commission (the Commission) lodged an F.I.R. with Gulshan Police Station against the petitioners under section 4 of the Money Laundering Protirodh Ain, 2009 and section 4 of Money Laundering Protirodh Ain, 2012 alleging that they had laundered 3,95,62,541.65/-U$D and 1,36,45,538.37/- HKD, thereby, committed offence under the aforesaid provisions of law. After holding investigation, the Investigating Officer submitted final report. The case was registered as Metropolitan Special Case No.80 of 2016 in the Court of Metropolitan Senior Special Judge, Dhaka. On 29.03.2016, the Metropolitan Senior Special Judge, Dhaka fixed 05.04.2016 for consideration of the said police report. On 05.04.2016, the Special Judge discharged the petitioners from the case upon accepting the said final report. Thereafter, on 29.05.2016, the Commission filed an application in the Court of Metropolitan Senior Special Judge under section 173(3B) of the Code of Criminal Procedure read with sections 19 and 20 of the Durnity Daman Commission Ain, 2004 for holding further investigation of the case. On 31.05.2016, the Commission also filed a ‘naraji’ petition against the final report submitted by the Investigating Officer. The Special Judge examined one Md. Zahangir Alam on behalf of the Commission. On 02.06.2016, the Metropolitan Senior Special Judge, Dhaka rejected the naraji petition as well as the application for holding further investigation filed by the Commission holding that after discharging the accused petitioners from the case upon accepting the final report, the said Court has became functus officio, so the ‘naraji’ petition was not entertainable.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The Commission then filed an application under section 10(1)(A) of the Criminal Law Amendment Act, 1958 in the High Court Division against the order dated 02.06.2016 and obtained Rule.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The High Court Division by its judgment and order dated 09.11.2016 finally disposed of the said Rule upon setting aside the order dated 05.04.2016 passed by the learned Metropolitan Senior Special Judge observing that the Anti Corruption Commission is at liberty to hold further investigation and in that regard no formal order is needed from the Court as per provision of section 173(7B) of the Code of Criminal Procedure. It also passed an order of freezing the wealth, in question, till 31.03.2017.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Against the said order, the petitioners have filed this Criminal Petition for Leave to Appeal.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mr. Rokanuddin Mahmud, learned Senior Counsel appearing for the petitioners, submits that the Commission challenged the legality and propriety of the order dated 02.06.2016 passed by the Special Judge rejecting the prayer for further investigation but the High Court Division set aside the order dated 05.04.2016 inasmuch as the said order was not challenged. He further submits that the petitioners got final report which was duly approved by the Commission and the Special Public Prosecutor did not raise any objection against the report when the same was taken up for consideration. Thus, the Special Judge, accepting the final report, discharged the petitioners. In such view of the matter, there is no error in the order of rejection of the application for further investigation.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mr. Khurshed Alam Khan, learned Counsel appearing for the Anti Corruption, submits that section 173(3B) of the Code of Criminal Procedure authorizes the investigation agencies to hold further investigation even without any sanction of the Court and that the order of discharge is not an order of acquittal so there is no bar for holding further investigation, the High Court Division upon correct appreciation of the law observed that no formal order is needed for the investigating agencies to hold further investigation over the matter.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The provision of further investigation is comprehended under section 173 (3B) of the Code of Criminal Procedure is something which is the exclusive prerogative of the investigation agencies. The provision does not, in specific terms, mention about any power of the Court to order further investigation. Section 156 of the Code of Criminal Procedure uses the expression ‘investigation’ only and not ‘further investigation’. No doubt, where there is already an investigation culminating in a police report, the court can trigger into motion the power of the police to conduct further investigation under section 173(3B) of the Code of Criminal Procedure. The said provision does not provide any specific provision that in order to hold further investigation by the police, it is necessary to take permission of the Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the case of Abdur Rahman Vs. State reported in 29 DLR(SC) 256, it was observed, </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“In the instant case the police took up investigation of the case, the offence alleged being a cognizable one. But the complainant himself as well as the witnesses were not available as they were, according to the police report, either hiding them or crossed over to India. Hence the police did not consider it expedient to keep the investigation in the case pending and submitted a final report whereupon the Magistrate discharged the accused who was in custody. However, after the lapse of sometime the police submitted an application to the Magistrate for starting reinvestigation of the case on the ground that evidence was available and it was forthcoming, whereupon the Magistrate allowed the prayer, vide order dated 09.04.1973. After investigation the police submitted the charge sheet upon which the Magistrate took cognizance of the offence and the appellant was thereafter apprehended. We think that in doing so, neither the police nor the Magistrate acted without jurisdiction.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the Case of Dr. H.B.M. Iqbal Vs. the State reported 12 MLR (AD) 30 this Division observed that there is no legal bar on further investigation and submission of supplementary charge sheet upon collection of additional evidence after submission of charge sheet or police report under Section 173(1) of the Code of Criminal Procedure. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The discharge of the accused on the basis of the final report does not amount to acquittal and so there is no bar of holding further investigation even after acceptance of police report when fresh material comes to light against accused persons. The investigating agency can not keep quiet. The words, ‘nothing is this section shall be deemed to preclude further investigation’ used in section 173(3B) clearly emphasize that nothing in Section 173 shall be construed to preclude further investigation by the investigating agency in respect of an offence after a report under section 173(1) of the Code. The Court can order for further investigation even after acceptance of final report stating non-availability of the materials. Since the order of discharge neither amounts to an acquittal nor to a final order, the accused can be proceeded against for the same offence on the basis of supplementary report submitted on holding further investigation or on the basis of naraji petition filed by the informant/complainant. It is no longer res integra that the Court, if exigent to do so, to espouse the cause of justice, can trigger further investigation even after a final report is submitted under section 173(3B) of the Code.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In view of the aforesaid proposition of law, we are of the view that the investigation of crime is carried out dehors the mandate contained in the Code of Criminal Procedure containing sections 154-173 of the Code and that the further investigation is a statutory right of the investigating agency under section 173(3B). The High Court Division rightly allowed the investigating agency of holding further investigation even after submission of the police report and after acceptance of the same. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Considering the facts, circumstances and law related thereto, we do not find any wrong in the decision of the High Court Division which calls for any interference by this Division.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Thus, the leave petition is dismissed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 112%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Ed.</span></strong></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___September__18/Issue__SEPTEMBER_%2018(2)__Crl.%20P.%20164%20of%2017__Hasan%20Foez%20Siddique__AD__2.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">CRIMINAL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL NO.164 OF 2017.</span></u></strong></a><u></u></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(From the judgment and order dated 09.11.2016 passed by the High Court Division in Criminal Revision No.1062 of 2016.</span></p></div></div></div></div>
673	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Mrs. Rafia Akhter Baby Vs.  Bangladesh House Building Finance, (Md. Nuruzzaman, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Civil Revision No. 487 of 2012  </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. A.S.M. Rahmatullah, Advocate ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Mrs. Rafia Akhter Baby </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Bangladesh House Building Finance Corporation </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Code of Civil Procedure  </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-02</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(CIVIL REVISIONAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="border-collapse: collapse; height: 232px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" width="672"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 301.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -7.4pt 6.0pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Md. Nuruzzaman, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoHeading8" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -7.4pt 6.0pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">And</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in -7.4pt .0001pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">S. H. Md. Nurul Huda Jaigirdar, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> </strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">09.01.2018 and 14.01.2018</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 57.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___September__18/Issue%20__SEPTEMBER__18(2)__C.R.%20487%20of%2012___Md.%20Nuruzzaman%20J.__9.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 269.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mrs. Rafia Akhter Baby</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . Petitioner </span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Bangladesh House Building Finance Corporation</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . Opposite parties </span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;">Section 115</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Before amendment of the Code by Act XXIX of 2003 as a Higher Court the High Court Division can pass an order under section 115(1) of the Code in its discretion as a supervisory Court but after amendment of the Code in the year of 2003 the Court must </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">act insofar as it relates to any order challenged</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> before it in accordance with the provision as provided in section 115 (1) of the Code as a higher Court of revisional jurisdiction. In execution proceeding there is no scope to apply the inherent jurisdiction of the Court in favour of the petitioner when the petitioner has once again failed to repay the loan money as per his on admission and thereafter she did not act fairly as per his own volition. Section 151 can be invoked only to secure the ends of justice and to prevent the abuse of the process of the Court, however, we find in the events of the present case, the petitioner once again by filing application under section 151 tried to prevent the proceeding started in accordance with law instead of securing the ends of justice. We are, therefore, of the opinion that in rejecting an application under section 151 of the Code the executing Court committed no error of law.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">      </span>. . . (31)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 115</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The petitioner obviously can file an application challenging the proclamation and auction sale of the suit property if any material illegality, irregularities or any violation of provision of law if has been committed by the Court in the proceeding of the execution regarding the proclamation and auction sale but instead of that the petitioner filed an application under section 151 of the Code for repay the outstanding loan due to her.
