text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">21.08.2016</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 46.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___September__18/Issue__SEPTEMBER_%2018(2)__C.%20Review%20189%20of%2015__Md.%20Abdul%20Wahhab%20Miah__AD__3.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 302.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Suza Uddoula and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Petitioners</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">-Versus</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Arshad Hossain Haider and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Respondents</span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">The Births, Deaths and </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Marriages Registration Act, (VI of 1886)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="color: #000000;">Section 13</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">It is clear that this Court did not deem it proper or in other words, did not feel it safe to rely on the death certificate issued by Dhaka City Corporation (exhibit 19), on the </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">ground that though Md. Jamiruddin allegedly</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> died on 13.04.1973, his death was recorded on 17.11.1991 long after filing the suit in 1986 without any explanation. . . . (16)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Evidence Act (I of 1872)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 35</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">As in the instant case, the delay in registering the information of death of Md. Jamiruddin was given long after 18 years and that again after the institution of the suit in 1986 without any explanation. To believe or disbelieve a document by a Court or refusal by a Court to rely on a particular document is dependent upon the appreciation of the evidence adduced in a particular case as well as its facts and circumstances, and a Court has every right either to believe or disbelieve a document or to rely or not to rely on a document subject to giving reason(s) by it for such believe or disbelieve or non-reliance. . . . (17)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908) </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Order XLVII, Rule 1(1)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Supreme Court of Bangladesh (Appellate Division) Rules, 1988</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Order XXVI, Rule 1</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">It does not require any elaboration to state the law that review is not rehearing of an appeal or to give a defeating party chance to start a second innings and the reasons given by a Court in not relying upon an exhibit in a case do not definitely come within the phraseology "or on account of some mistake or error apparent on the face of the record" within the meaning of rule 1(1) of Order XLVII of the Code of Civil Procedure read with rule 1 of Order XXVI of The Supreme Court of Bangladesh, (Appellate Division) Rules 1988.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">           </span>. . . (18)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; letter-spacing: -.3pt; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For the Appellants:</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mr. Abdul Wadud Bhuiyan, Senior Advocate, with Mr. Nurul Amin, Senior Advocate, intructed by Mrs. Madhumalati Chy. Barua, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For Respondents:</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Mr. Shamsul Haque, Advocate instructed by Mr. Syed Mahbabur Rahman, Advocate-on-Record. </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J</span></u></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">:</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">This Civil Review Petition has been filed by the plaintiffs for reviewing the judgment passed by this Court on the 20<sup>th</sup> day of November, 2014 in Civil Appeal No.189 of 2010 allowing the same.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The said appeal arose out of the judgment and order dated the 14<sup>th</sup> day of May 2009, passed by the High Court Division in Civil Revision No.3839 of 2001 making the Rule absolute.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The predecessor of petitioner Nos.1-3 and petitioner NO.4 as the plaintiffs filed Title Suit NO.339 of 1986 in the First Court of Senior Assistant Judge, Dhaka for declaration of title and for recovery of Khas possession of the suit property impleading the present respondents as the defendants. The plaintiff’s case, in short, was that the suit property measuring 5 kathas land equivalent to more or less 8 decimals was allotted to Md. Jamiruddin by a deed of settlement date 27.07.1953 by the then Government of East Pakistan. Md. Jamiruddin constructed a semi-pucca house on the allotted land and resided therin with his family members. He paid rents and taxes of the Union Parishad. On 01.06.1968, Md. Jamiruddin applied to the concerned authority for issuing clearance certificate to construct a two storied building as per approved plan of the then DIT and the authority issued a clearance certificate on 21.07.1968. While owning and possessing the suit property, Md. Jamiruddin being in need of cash money proposed to sell the same to the plaintiffs in the first week of March, 1971. The plaintiffs agreed to purchase the suit property for a consideration of Tk.40,000.00. On 12.03.1971, Md. Jamiruddin on receipt of Tk.20,000.00 from the plaintiffs executed a bainapatra in favour of plaintiff NO.1. As per stipulation of the said binapatra, the sale was required to be completed within 3 years from the date of the bainapatra. After that Jamiruddin died on 13.04.1973 leaving behind his only son Nasiruddin as his heir. While owning possessing the suit property, Nasiruddin admitted the liability of his late father under the said bainapatra as he was an attesting witness thereto. On several occasions, Md. Jamiruddin received part of the balance consideration money from the plaintiffs by putting his signatures on the back page of the said bainapatra. On 13.04.1985, Nasiruddin executed and registered the deed of sale in favour of the plaintiffs on receipt of the balance consideration of taka 11,500.00 and delivered physical possession of the suit property to them. Nasiruddin is a Bangladeshi National and he never opted for Pakistan. He obtained a succession certificate from the Third Court of Subordinate Judge, Dhaka, vide Succession Certificate Case No. 1011 of 1984. While the plaintiffs were in possession of the suit property, defendant No.1 with a group of men forcibly dispossessed them therefrom on 15.04.1986 on the plea that he purchased the suit property from one Rahim Bashak on 28.09.1977 by a registered deed of sale. Rahim Bashak was alleged to have purchased the suit property from Md. Jamiruddin by a deed of sale dated 23.04.1975. Md. Jamiruddin never sold the suit property to Rahim Bashak who never owned and possessed the same. The deed of sale alleged to have been executed and registered by Rahim Bashak was a forged and fabricated document. Defendant No. 1 did not acquire any right, title and interest in the suit property on the basis of the said deed. The plaintiffs acquired valid right, title and interest in the suit property by purchase from the lawful owner. Hence the plaintiffs were constrained to file the suit for the relief aforementioned.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Defendant No.1 died during the pendency of the suit and after his death the suit <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">was contested by his heirs respondent Nos.1-7 by </span></span><span style="font-size: 11pt;">filing written statement denying all the material statements made in the plaint. Their case, in short, was that the original allottee Md. Jamiruddin had transferred the suit property to Rahim Bashak by a registered deed of sale dated 23.05.1975. Rahim Bashak subsequently, transferred the suit property to their father deceased defendant No.1 by a registered deed of sale dated 28.09.1977. Since purchase their father had been living in the suit property by constructing houses and some portion of the suit property has been let out to the tenants. After getting settlement from the then Government of East been residing therein. On the prayer of Jamiruddin the then DIT issued a clearance certificate in his favour on 21.07.1968 who constructed a building on the suit property. After transferring the suit property to Rahim Bashak, Md. Jasimuddin had been residing at 11/6 Bakshi Bazar lane. The defendants got their names mutated and have been paying rents and taxes regularly. The defendants have been in possession of the suit property and the plaintiffs did not have any possession therein. The defendants never dispossessed the plaintiffs from the suit property. The plaintiffs' title deed was false and forged and they (the defendants) had right, title and interest in the suit property. The suit was filed making false statements and as such, the same was liable to be dismissed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">5.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The trial Court by its judgment and decree dated 30.09.1998 dismissed the suit. Against the judgment and decree of the trial Court, the plaintiffs preferred Title Appeal No.406 of 1998 before the District Judge, Dhaka. The learned Additional District Judge, Third Court, Dhaka, by his judgment and decree dated 08.04.2001 dismissed the appeal and affirmed those of the trial Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">6.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the judgment and decree of the Appellate Court, the plaintiffs moved the High Court Division by filing a revision application and obtained the Rule in Civil Revision No.3839 of 2001.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">7.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">A learned Judge of the Single Bench by the judgment and order dated 14.05.2009 made the Rule absolute and decreed the suit.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">8.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Against the judgment and order of the High Court Division, the defendant respondents filed Civil Petition for leave to Appeal No.96 of 2010 and leave was granted on 04.02.2010 giving rise to Civil Appeal No. 198 of 2010. And this Court by the judgment sought to be reviewed allowed the appeal.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">9.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Heard Mr. Abdul Wadud Bhuiyan and Mr. Nurul Amin, the learned Counsel for the petitioners and Mr. Shamsul Haque, learned Counsel who entered caveat on behalf of the defendant-respondents</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">10.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">From the pleading of the respective party it is apparent that the controversies in the suit were (a) whether Md. Jamiruddin, the original allotte of the suit property entered in to an agreement with the plaintiffs on 12.03.1971 to sell the same, (b) whether Md. Jamiruddin died on 13.04.1973 leaving behind Nasriuddin, a son as his only heir and (c) whether Nasiruddin could execute and register the sale deed in favour of the plaintiffs in respect of the suit property.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">11.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">This Court in the judgment sought to be reviewed noticed that the High Court Division found that the defendants neither in their written statement nor in their deposition claimed that the bainapatra was not executed by Md. Jamiruddin and that Nasiruddin was not his son and that Nasiruddin did not execute and register the deed of sale in favour of the plaintiffs as the son of the original allottee Md. Jamiruddin and then discarded the said findings of the High Court Division with the finding as under:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.35pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">"The above findings of the High Court Division are contrary to the statements made by the defendants in their written statement. In paragraph-10 of the written statement, the defendants stated, amongst others, that </span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">ÓD³ †gvt RwgiDwÏb Kw¯§KKv‡jI ev`xc‡ÿi mwnZ †Kvb evqbvcÎ m¤úv`b K‡i bvBÓ </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">and in paragraph-12 stated, amongst others, that</span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> ÓD³ †gvt RwgiDwÏ‡bi bvwmiDwÏb bv‡g †Kvb cyÎ wQj bv ev bvB| myZivs Zvnv‡K evsjv‡`‡k ivwLqv hvIqvi cÖkœ I‡V bv Ges ZZ Øviv †Kvb `wjj m¤úv`‡biI ckœ I‡V bv|Ó</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Defendant No.l-(ka) as D.W-1 deposed that it was not a fact that Md. Jamiruddin entered into a contract with the plaintiffs and that the bainapatra (exhibit-8) was forged and collusive and that the signature of Md. jamiruddin was forged and that Md. Jamiruddin did not have a son named Nasiruddin. Admittedly, the plaintiffs could not prove the alleged bainapatra (exhibit-8) by producing any attesting witnesses thereof."</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">12.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The learned Counsel for the petitioners failed to show with reference to the written statement and the deposition of DW-1 that the above quoted findings of this Court are the result of improper consideration of the facts stated in the written statement and the deposition of DW-1 or is otherwise perverse.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">13.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The High Court Division in coming to the finding that Md. Jamiruddin died on 14.03.1973, relied upon exhibit 19, the death certificate dated 18.11.1991 issued by Dhaka City Corporation and this Court did not consider it proper to rely upon exhibit 19 on the reasoning that according to the plaintiffs Md. Jamiruddin died on 13.04.1973 and his death was recorded on 17.11.1991, that registration of death of Jamiruddin was made long after filing the suit in 1986 without any explanation. We do not see any prima-facic wrong in the above reasoning given by this Court in not relying upon exhibit-19.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">14.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">If further appears that the High Court Division relied upon exhibit-13, the certificate issued by the graveyard authority. This Court noticed that the Appellate Court having considered the certificate came to the finding that <em>"under what authority the Vice-Chair man of Relief Committee issued that certificate was not comprehensible and that the Vice-Chairman of the Relief Committee did not have the authority to issue such certificate. "</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">15.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The learned counsel for the petitioners could not show any law or any other legal instrument authorizing the vice-chairman of the Relief Committee to issue such certificate to nullify the above quoted finding of the Appellate Court. However, they tried to rely upon the death certificate of Md. Jamiruddin issued by Dhaka City Corporation by referring to section 13 of the Registration of Births and Deaths Act, 1969 (the Act, 1969) and the connected rule submitting that mere delay in registering the information of death of a person with the registering authority, as happened in the instant case, shall not make such register and the certificate of such death registry issued by a proper authority invalid or inadmissible in evidence They have submitted that according to section 13 of the Act, 1969 for the delay in registering the information of death of a person, one is to pay late fee depending on the period of delay in giving such information and also subject to observance of other procedure/ formalities and in the instant case the death certificate having been given by the competent authority, this Court committed an error apparent on the face of the judgment in refusing to rely upon the them and as such, the same needs to be reviewed.</span></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___September__18/Issue__SEPTEMBER_%2018(2)__C.%20Review%20189%20of%2015__Md.%20Abdul%20Wahhab%20Miah__AD__3.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Civil </span></u></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Review Petition No. 189 OF 2015.</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(From the judgment and order dated the 20th day of November, 2014 passed by the Appellate Division in Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No.189 of 2010)</span></p></div></div></div></div>
676	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">The State Vs. Begum Khaleda Zia, (Muhammad Imman Ali, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL PETITION FOR  LEAVE TO APPEAL  No. 621 OF 2018  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Syed Mahmud Hossain, CJ,  Muhammad Imman Ali, J, Hasan Foez Siddique, J Mirza Hussain Haider, J.  </p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division  ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Mahbubey Alam, Attorney General with Mr. Biswajit Debnath, Deputy Attorney General instructed by Mrs. Sufia Khatun, Advocate-on-Record ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ (AD)      </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  The State  </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Begum Khaleda Zia </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Code of Criminal Procedure  </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-02</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112px;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The State </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Petitioner </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">-Versus</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Begum Khaleda Zia</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Respondent</span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Code of Criminal Proce</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">dure (V of 1898)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;">Section 498</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">There is no doubt that the power to grant bail under section 498 of the Code is given both to the High Court Division as well as the Court of Sessions. In the decision reported in 10 DLR 541 it was held that a revision application direct to the High Court Division is not ordinarily entertainable. A different view appears in the case reported in 24 BLD (AD) 168. However, in the instant case this issue of the maintainability has not been finally adjudicated by the High Court Division. The ends of justice would be best served if the High Court Division is directed </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">to adjudicate upon the issue of maintainability</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> while disposing of the Rule issued in respect of the bail of accused-respondent.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                     </span>...(6 and 7)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Shah Zillur Rahman Mutawalli Vs. The State, 10 DLR 541 and The State Vs. Md. Nurul Islam @ Babul, 24 BLD (AD) 168 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For the Petitioner:</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Mahbubey Alam, Attorney General with Mr. Biswajit Debnath, Deputy Attorney General instructed by Mrs. Sufia Khatun, Advocate-on-Record</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For Respondent:</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Khandakar Mahbub Hossain, Senior Advocate with Mr. A.J. Mohammad Ali, Senior Advocate with Jainul Abedin, Senior Advocate with Mr. A.M. Mahbududdin, Advocate with Mr. Sogir Hossain, Advocate instructed by Mr. Zainul Abedin, Advocate-on-Record</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><h4 style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 24.0pt;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-variant: small-caps; mso-font-width: 110%;">Muhammad Imman Ali, J</span></u><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">:</span></u> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">This criminal petition for leave to appeal is directed against the order dated 28.05.2018 passed by a Division Bench of the High Court Division in Criminal Miscellaneous Case No.25897 of 2018 granting ad-interim bail for a period of 6(six) months in GR Case No.51 of 2015 arising out of Choddogram PS Case No.04 dated 03.02.2015 under sections 149/302/ 326/324 /427/109/34 of the Penal Code, now pending before the Court of Chief Judicial Magistrate, Cumilla.</span></h4><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The respondent, Begum Khaleda Zia was shown arrested in the abovementioned case on 08.04.2018 and on 10.04.2018, an application for bail filed before the cognizance Court, Cumilla was rejected, whereupon the accused-respondent filed Criminal Miscellaneous Case No.2518 of 2018 before the Session Judge, Cumilla on 16.04.2018. By order dated 23.04.2018, the learned Sessions Judge fixed 07.06.2018 for further hearing of the bail matter. On 07.06.2018, the application for bail was dismissed as not pressed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">In the meantime, the accused-respondent filed Criminal Miscellaneous Case No.25897 of 2018 before the High Court Division praying for bail. By the impugned Order, the High Court Division issued Rule and granted ad-interim bail to the accused-respondent for a period of 6(six) months. Hence, the State has filed the instant criminal petition for leave to appeal.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Mahbubey Alam, learned Attorney General, appearing on behalf of the petitioner submitted that the bail application filed before the Sessions Judge in Criminal Miscellaneous Case No.2518 of 2018 was dismissed as not pressed and hence, there is no application for bail before the Sessions Judge. The accused-respondent filed a criminal miscellaneous Case for bail before the High Court Division, which has concurrent jurisdiction in such matter under section 498 of the Code of Criminal Procedure (the Code). However, he submitted, by reference to the Full Bench decision in the case of Shah Zillur Rahman Mutawlli –VS- The State 10 DLR 541, that a revisional application must be moved before the Sessions Judge and “a revision application direct to the High Court Division is not ordinarily entertainable.” He submitted that the decision in the case of the State -Vs- Md. Nurul Islam @ Babul, 24, BLD (AD) 168 is distinguishable in the facts and circumstances of the instant case, inasmuch as in that case this Division found that keeping the bail matter pending for hearing in spite of persistent prayers for bail tantamount to refusal of bail, whereas in the instant case the bail application was dismissed as not pressed. There was no final decision on merit. He further submitted that since the High Court Division <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">has not finally disposed of the Rule, the question</span> of maintainability of the miscellaneous case filed before the High Court Division will be decided there.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Khandakar Mahbub Hossain, learned Senior Advocate with Mr. A.J. Mohammad Ali, learned Senior Advocate with Mr. Jainul Abedin, learned Senior Advocate with Mr. A.M. Mahbubuddin, learned Advocate and Mr. Sogir Hossain, learned Advocate instructed by Mr. Zainul Abedin, learned Advocate-on-Record, appearing on behalf of the respondent submitted that the accused-respondent is entitled to get the benefit of the provision to section 497 of the Code being a woman aged 73 years and also being a sick and infirm person. He further submitted that the jurisdiction of the High Court Division to hear an application for bail under section 498 of the Code is concurrent to that of the Court of Sessions. He further submitted that in the case of the State -Vs- Md. Nurul Islam @ Babul, 24, BLD (AD) 168, it was held that the lower Court should be moved first, but it is not an inviolable biblical rule. In exceptional circumstances, the Higher Court can also be moved, and hence, the High Court Division did not commit any error in entertaining the application and granting ad-interim bail to the accused-respondent.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">There is no doubt that the power to grant bail under section 498 of the Code is given both to the High Court Division as well as the Court of Sessions. the decision reported in 10 DLR cited above has been brought to our notice, where it was held that a revision application direct to the High Court Division is not ordinarily entertainable. A different view appears in the case reported in 24 BLD. However, in the instant case this issue of the maintainability has not been finally adjudicated by the High Court Division/</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">In such facts and circumstances, we are of the view that the ends of justice would be best served if the High Court Division is directed to adjudicate upon the issue of maintainability while disposing of the Rule issued in respect of the bail of the accused-respondent.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the discussion above, the instant criminal petition for leave to appeal is disposed of. The Division Bench presided over by AKM Asaduzzaman, J is directed to dispose of the Rule within 4 (four) weeks from date. The order of stay granted by the learned Judge-in-Chamber shall continue till disposal of the Rule.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Ed.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"> </span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___September__18/Issue__SEPTEMBER_%2018(2)__Crl.%20P.%20621%20of%2018__Muhammad%20Imman%20Ali__AD__1.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">CIVIL PETITION FOR<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>LEAVE TO APPEAL<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>No. 621 OF 201</span></u></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">8.</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(From the judgement and order dated 28<sup>th</sup> of May, 2018 passed by the High Court Division in Criminal Miscellaneous Case No.25897).</span></p></div></div></div></div>
